<Review>My family had dessert here in August 2013 and absolutely loved the ice cream.  My 4 year hold inhaled his chocolate peanut butter scoop and came up asking for more.  My 2 year old liked his raspberry sorbet (one of two options they have with no egg).

But of course two young kids liked the ice cream.  The more discriminating palates belonged to my wife's parents, both of whom raved about the quality of the ice cream.  So, we'll go back.

One interesting thing they have posted on the wall is an invitation to purchase "the world's most expensive cup of ice cream."  For $60,000 the founder will hand make you all the ice cream you can eat from one of the disappearing glaciers on the summit of Mt. Kilimanjaro.  The idea is to call attention to global warming and the impact it is having on these glaciers.  Is it too wonky and ornery of me to point out that the shrinkage of those particular glaciers has nothing to do with CO2, but is rather due to changes in weather patters resulting from deforestation in the areas surrounding the mountain?  In any case, kudos to these guys for the clever idea.< /Review>< resp>

<username>Merisa M< /username><review>If there was an Ice Cream King, Three Twins Ice Cream would be wearing the crown. She and I had just eaten a huge lunch at a Taste of the Himalayas and were looking for a place to burn off some calories.  We mozied downtown and discovered the Oxbow Public Market (my new favorite food destination in Napa).  Instead of burning off calories we ended up taking more than our fair share in. < Text>
After seeing the "Carl Van" in Fairfield, I decided that this is a Ice Cream I needed to try. So I headed to Vacaville and the Nugget Market: I knew they would have the Three Twins. And sure enough, I found the Twins. The selection was meager, with Vanilla, Mint Confeti and the cookie type. Digging into the back for the hardest, frozen container, I chose the Mint. That night after dinner we opened the container for the first time. We found the ice cream not creamy in appearance, but rather the consistency of ice milk, as if cream was not in it. Scooping into a cooled dish, the ice milk broke apart into liquid, chocolate chips, and crystals of a white mass. Tasting was not any better. It tasted milky, minty and ice chip crispy  We did not get the experience of  high quality ice cream that you get from Lourdes, Ben and Jerry's, Coldstone or  a commercial produced product.

I give Three Twin's Ice Cream a rating of 2 on a scale of 10. It is no better the ice milk.<//Text>

<name>Peter Petey Pete< /name><date>1496192515033</date>< Rate>
3</Rate>
< review>
Not bad. Not amazing.

Had the spicy tonkotsu level 2 spice level. I added corn, butter, egg and 4 extra slices of chashu. I should have bumped up to spice level 3 or 4 as level 2 just had a spicy flavor and not actual heat. Still pretty good flavor with a bit too much sodium. The noodles were thin. The egg was cooked to a dry yolk consistency. The slices of chashu were thinly sliced. It melted in the broth and in your mouth.

Overall it's not bad, we didn't have to wait compared to a long line for some of the other ramen spots nearby. Service was quick and kind. Being as my friend lives close by, I'll be back to try some other offerings in hopes of finding something delicious.</review>

<UserId.>107433150273567804942</UserId.>< user_name>
Dane Jacobson<//user_name>
<time>1523816779854<//time><rate>5< /rate>< review>
In an area (the greater South Bay region) that can be prone to pretense and frills, it's nice to find a veterinary group that provides good service for good value.

We have been taking our dog here for almost a year now, since we first got him as a puppy. We've had nothing but good service - and he's been through a lot! His ear was mauled by a husky and required surgical repair. He had his neuter here. He also had an umbilical hernia repair. He came to us with worms and fleas that they helped us rid. They've also provided guidance in avoiding spending too much of our money on ridiculously expensive dog foods. (He's spoiled enough as it is!)

This place is not a boutique-style veterinary office with fancy flat panel LED TVs. They don't particularly push you to buy any of the few products they sell there, except of course any prescription medications your pet might need. Even when prescribing medications, they try to go for the cheapest, most effective option. They've even passed forward manufacturer rebates for oral deworming medication.

Overall, I really can't recommend this place enough. We've a healthy, awesome puppy and don't feel like I'm being manipulated everytime I go to the vet.< /review>

< Review>
I have been here twice, and ordered the chaufa with chicken both times. Its basically a fried rice dish and delicious. It is served with a spicy green sauce, and I asked what was in the sauce and was told it was a secret. The filet mignon empanadas were very good also. Try the purple corn beverage.  It reminds me of jamaica , but incorporates a cinnamon flavor. I've yet to travel to Peru but I feel based on the offerings here I wouldn't have to worry about the food when I got there! They have patio seating for dine in.< /Review>

<name>Chris Branch< /name><Time>1618851427349< /Time><rate>5<//rate><review>It's good</review><pictures>None< /pictures><resp>None< /resp><Gmap_id>0x80c32901696e0843:0x5d24d408a4b5323b<//Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
<username>Mar E< /username>< pics>
None</pics>
<Text>Considering the conditions that we are living in, I must say that most eateries have done a great job adapting to the circumstances. With this being said, I recommend we, as a community, continue supporting small businesses in this time of Covid. As for Misky, it's take out food was delicious, as it had been pre-Covid. The spices (flavoring) are in line with past meals in-house; the ceviche-just as fresh, lemony, tender morsels of yum; the lomo saltado with it's pungent onions and bell peppers & french fries sopping up all the juices released from the protein & veg--still delicioso. All these flavor profiles remeniscent of carefree months long ago. The chicken chaufa and green rice have been more flavorful in the past, but overall not too disappointing. I'm glad this family owned restaurant didn't go the way side and shutter it's doors for good (like other local places), and there is comfort  knowing that I can anticipate ordering more goodness and it won't be a disappointment. I would suggest ordering by phone ahead and tack on 15 minutes to their projected wait time, because this place is still as popular as ever. There is no delivery available (bummed, but ok) at this time (as of 7/31). The patio area is on the smallish side, but it is open for dining-al-fresco, and you'll have to order first, pay and then be seated. Please be patient with the staff there aren't many servers to keep pace, but that's out of the abundance to maximize their earnings & expenses. BE WELL, WEAR YOUR MASK, and I'll be seeing you on the gastronomic highway of life.< /Text>< resp>
None<//resp>

< text>
Today we went to Misky Misky  to celebrate Father's Day, so sad to see how the food and service is not up to were they used to be.  I understand that things have changed that we need to adhered to the changes but it was very disappointing.

First you have to decide as you enter what you are going to eat and drink, pay and then choose your table (awful).  It took over 20 minutes for someone to bring the drinks that were already prepared and in top of the counter.  No one brought silverware and napkins until we asked, usually they place on the table toasted salted corn with sauces as a courtesy, today they charged for it.  Then it took another 40 minutes and  they brought the food, the rice wasn't completely cooked, the appetizers came after the main dishes and the anticuchos were super thin, dry and over cooked, the potatoes a la huancahina was one potato cut in 5 slices with a little bit of a sauce that didn't have any flavor.  I couldn't believe the service, they never brought the water that we requested when we entered, the server "never" came to check if we needed refills on the coffee and drinks.  I have been going to this restaurant since they opened and never disappointed today was ridiculously bad and the place was not even close to be full, what a waist of $120 we won't be coming back.  We have gone to other restaurants and even though they have to maintain social distancing the food and service have improved because they want patrons to come back sorry to say Misky Misky is not trying to give their patrons a good dinning experience at this time.< /text>

<Rating>5<//Rating>< review>
Great place for Peruvian food. Came here to see how they compare to Mr. Pollo couple miles away. Turns out same owners. The ceviche was really fresh. We also got the Tallarin Verde con Bistek and the Lomo Saltado which were both really good. The steaks were really tender and flavorful. The fries in the Lomo Saltado was a bit over fried and was too hard. As far as service goes, there was only two servers and so service was a bit slow. We ended up having to flag down the server at the end of the meal to get the check.

Overall, I think I'd go to Mr. Pollo if I want a quick bite, especially since they have a really awesome chimchirri sauce that wasn't at Misky Misky. But if you have a large group, then definitely go to Misky Misky as they have a larger dining area.</review>

<response>None<//response>< Review>
I had never had Peruvian food and decided to give this place a try after having passed it many times. Checked it out on TA, found very favorable reviews, and off I went on a Thursday evening. It was close to 7:00pm on a weekenight, but 3/4 filled with people enjoying themselves. It is not fancy inside, nor is it plain. The ambience is casual and very friendly. The menu has plenty of choices and many of the dishes come in your choice of fish, chicken or beef. I had a shredded chicken in a delicious sauce over wonderful potatoes...and big mound of very flavorful rice on the side. Yup, potatoes and rice. As many other TA reviewers have noted, it works! The portion was fine; some of the other dishes had very large portions. Bottom line, do not be afraid to try this cuisine if it is new to you. The dishes are like good comfort food, nothing that should in any way scare off a timid palate. You will like it. Everyone I talk to who has gone, does. And the prices are terrific.</Review>

<Resp>None<//Resp><name>Jared Cohee</name>< review>
PERÃš ðŸ‡µðŸ‡ª
Excerpt from Eat the World Los Angeles:
Two things are immediately apparent right when you open the door. The first is on the big board, a list of ceviches that are the pride and joy of the restaurant. The second is an enjoyable atmosphere and energy that can almost make your skin tingle in anticipation when walking in.

Much of the menu and dish descriptions here go out of the way to focus on and promote the products and culture of PerÃº. You will see "Peruvian" in front of many items you thought you already knew, like passion fruit and corn. One of those distinctly Peruvian corns comes before any meal in the form of cancha (above), a toasted snack that pairs well with just about any drink and really gets the taste buds ready.

The ceviche selected from the big board on this day was ceviche de mango ($18, below), which combines shrimp, mussels, scallops, and squid with the fish of the day in a marinade kissed by aji amarillo. Somehow the chunks of mango hid from the camera, but you can see both hominy and more cancha, as well as a big hunk of sweet potato that almost tastes of pumpkin pie. Those that have had Peruvian ceviches before will recognize the seaweed, which is also imported from PerÃº and very distinct.< /review>

<review>The food here was absolutely amazing.

I only tried two dishes while I was here. I had the Seco Combinado, which was amazing. The beef was tender and the flavors were great. Best yet, the rice was absolutely phenomenal. I was in love with it and I would order the rice by itself.

The other dish I tried was the Chaufa de Pollo. I wasn't sold on it at first because I don't normally like fried rice, but I have to say that it exceeded expectations and it was probably the best fried rice I've had.

The interior was fresh, modern, and most importantly clean. The staff was friendly and helpful.

Overall, I definitely recommend this restaurant and I will be back!< /review>< date>

<user_name>Gerso Guillen<//user_name><Date>1555476802811</Date>< rate>

< review>
My first time here was a nice experience because I had ordered cheviche to go for my wife but when we got here my wife changed her mind so the host was nice enough to offer for us to sit at the bar. It was a nice gesture on his part.

Tonight my cousin who is visiting from VA wanted to eat Peruvian food so I thought of this place plus I wanted to try a dish I had seen which is a layer of potatoes, layer of avocado a layer of egg and a layer of chicken I think. Anyways I ordered also a glass of purple sangria.  We were left unattended for a really long time.  I think because there was two big party groups that more important to the workers.  So after a really long wait we get our drinks and I wondered since when did purple turn to orange colored.  I asked the lady what happened she oops we will get you the correct drink.  They bring the food except I have no plate in front of me so I waited to see if it was late or what.  I then started to feel they forgot about me... So I asked she goes back there and she come back and states that they messed up on the dish so they could not make it anymore.  I asked what they messed up, she then says if I want anything else.  I told her no.  I got up a little bit later and as I saw all a man that looked like he worked there.  I asked him to not charge us for any of the food I ordered as I didn't get nor did the workers get my drink right.  To please allow my cousin to enjoy her food and that was all.  The guy agreed.

So hit or miss what can I tell you.  Service might be there and it might not be there at all.  Food is great don't get me wrong just be ready to be ignored if they have big parties.< /review>

I ate here based upon the prior reviews and can verify that all are very â€œspot onâ€. The food was very good as was the service. <Text>I've been to Peru before and I know how good Lomo Soltado taste like. So when my girlfriend took me here, I was a little doubtful that it may not measure up to the Lomo Soltado I ate in Peru. The waitress was nice and friendly and immediately show us our table. It wasn't busy when we got there but started to get busy right after we left. Our waitress took the time to explain the dishes and the ceviches. I ordered the Pollo Lomo Soltado and my girlfriend ordered the beef. The preparation of the dish looks different from the Lomo Soltado in Peru ( the French fries were mixed with the dish as opposed to putting it on the side). My first taste told me, Yum!!!! I liked it a lot and I am happy. It brought me back to Peru in my imagination. So, so good!! The tomato and onion was not over-cooked and was quite good. Our waitress was attentive and help us pack our left-over food (the dish was too much for me). The restaurant appeared clean. I will be back here.</Text>< pictures>

<name>Luis P.< /name><Date>1483756602965</Date>< rate>
2</rate>
<Text>First of all: not because a place has a big shinning, and the cooking staff wearing black chef outfits, makes for good eating. How many times, I, myself, have prepared a delicious meal at home, only to put forth a series of blunders in subsequent attempts? Too many to count, that is for sure, because excellent cooking is a rarity, not the norm.
Misky Misky presently enjoys 4 solid stars in Yelp, which for better or for worst, is the site many good people utilized to determine where they may want to go eat. They charged a pretty penny for their dishes, and even though there are many things to admire of their location, the food, I am here to tell, is definitely their strong suit. To be frank, is an affront to the truly wonderful Peruvian Cuisine, and I will go one step further by saying that Peruvian food in USA, is a series of missteps, and below part effort. Uneven, expensively disappointing, and a bad example of the real deal. How do I voice such a harsh opinion? I have spent hundreds, more like thousands of dollars, eating at countless so called Peruvian establishments, and if by luck I ate very well at one or the other, the next time the experience plummeted to mediocre. Misky Misky is not all that good. Plates:
AjÃ­ de Gallina, $9 (lunch time special): a creamy sauce made with yellow Peruvian Chili with shredded chicken, served with rice-the do give you a significant mound of decent white rice, if only white rice was the main dish, they would probably deserve their fake 4 stars rating-and potatoes, boil egg, and black seeded olive. In Peru, a masterpiece in every way, In West Covina average at best. 3 Stars.
Papa a la Huancaina, $8. Potatoes served with a velvety sauce, really delicious. Garnished with olives and boil egg. Misky version a disaster in texture, flavor, and value. 2 Stars.
Pollo a la Anticuchera, $10. A flat, thin piece of chicken, dried beyond redemption, like a shoe sole I would compare it to, with salad and the mound of rice. Good job, Chefs! Thanks for water to be able to swallow this concoction. 1 Star.
Cau Cau de Mariscos, $15. Let's just say that the seafood part was overshadowed by the overwhelming amount of potatoes. Sauce runny and devoid of any taste. Rice better than the rest. $15 frigging dollars?! 1 Star.
Fried Calamari, $12? Heavy on the oil, excessive breading. We are not in the right place for a delicate dish such as this one. 1.5 Star.
Ceviche Mixto, $16. The signature dish of Peru. This version very small, but must admit it was good. The mixed seafood tasted fine. 4 Stars.
Water with very little after taste, service indifferent and turtle like slow. Yes, we drove 50+ miles, weather the LA traffic for this? Peruvian food anyone? Planes will take you to the Mecca, but here a series of misfortunes by being at the mercy of incompetent talentless cooks. No Chefs worth their money to be found so far, I don't care how many glowing reviews, do not believe the hype! $80 plus for a meal better prepared at home, for a fraction of the cost. 2 Stars.<//Text><pics>None<//pics>< response>
